{"parentUuid":null,"isSidechain":true,"promptId":"037faac4-a90e-48f6-9041-5732c00f999d","agentId":"a4168095d3318bdca","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":"Deep research on designing the risk engine software architecture for an algorithmic crypto trading system. The risk engine is the most safety-critical component.\n\nResearch thoroughly:\n\n1. **Risk engine as a separate process/service**:\n   - The trading engine should NOT be able to bypass the risk engine\n   - Design: risk engine wraps the exchange API — all orders go through it\n   - If risk engine crashes: ALL trading stops (fail-safe, not fail-open)\n   - Separation of concerns: trading logic in one process, risk in another\n   - Communication: shared memory, message queue, or function call?\n\n2. **Pre-trade risk checks** (before order submission):\n   - Position size within limits?\n   - Sufficient margin available?\n   - Not in kill switch state?\n   - Drawdown within acceptable range?\n   - Volatility within tradeable range?\n   - Data freshness acceptable?\n   - Model confidence above threshold?\n   - Daily/weekly loss budget remaining?\n   - Not too close to funding settlement?\n   - Order passes the check → submit; fails → log reason, reject\n\n3. **Post-trade risk monitoring** (continuous):\n   - Mark-to-market every tick/bar\n   - Distance to liquidation\n   - Unrealized PnL tracking\n   - Holding period tracking\n   - Maximum adverse excursion (MAE) tracking\n   - Kill switch condition monitoring\n\n4. **State management**:\n   - All risk state must persist to disk (SQLite or file)\n   - Kill switch states survive restart\n   - Position state survives restart\n   - Daily/weekly PnL counters reset at correct times\n   - State schema: what fields to track\n\n5. **Risk engine API design**:\n   ```python\n   class RiskManager:\n       def approve_trade(signal) -> TradeDecision\n       def on_fill(fill) -> None\n       def on_bar(bar) -> RiskActions  # may return \"close position\", \"reduce size\"\n       def get_state() -> RiskState\n       def reset_kill_switch(switch_name, auth_token) -> bool\n       def emergency_close_all() -> None\n   ```\n   What should each method do? What should it return? Error handling?\n\n6. **Fail-safe vs fail-open design**:\n   - Fail-safe: if anything goes wrong, STOP TRADING (this is correct)\n   - Fail-open: if risk check fails, allow the trade anyway (NEVER do this)\n   - Timeout handling: if risk check takes too long, default to REJECT\n   - Network failure: if can't reach exchange, default to NO NEW POSITIONS\n\n7. **Risk event logging**:\n   - Every risk decision must be logged with full context\n   - Why was a trade approved/rejected?\n   - What was the risk state at that moment?\n   - How to structure risk logs for post-mortem analysis\n   - Separate risk log file vs main application log\n\n8. **Risk alerts and notifications**:\n   - Priority levels: info, warning, critical, emergency\n   - Notification channels: log, webhook, Slack, PagerDuty, SMS\n   - What triggers each level?\n   - Alert fatigue management: don't spam alerts\n\n9. **Testing the risk engine**:\n   - Unit tests for each risk check\n   - Integration tests with simulated trading\n   - Chaos testing: what happens when components fail?\n   - Property-based testing: risk engine should NEVER approve a position that violates limits\n   - Fuzz testing: random signals → verify no limit violations\n\n10. **Risk engine performance**:\n    - Pre-trade checks must complete in <10ms (don't add latency)\n    - Post-trade monitoring must not block the main loop\n    - Memory management for state tracking\n    - Database write performance for risk event logging\n\n11. **Recovery from risk engine failure**:\n    - If risk engine crashes: trading process detects and halts\n    - Watchdog process that monitors risk engine health\n    - Automatic restart with state recovery from disk\n    - Manual override protocol (for emergencies only)\n\n12. **Risk engine configuration**:\n    - All limits configurable via config file (not hardcoded)\n    - Config changes require explicit reload (not hot-swap)\n    - Config validation: reject invalid risk parameters\n    - Audit trail for config changes\n\nFor each: design patterns, Python code, specific recommendations for our system, and failure mode analysis."},"uuid":"09eb88e5-48d4-44dd-b9c9-e53088633011","timestamp":"2026-03-23T13:29:39.926Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

ulthandler.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/_pytest/fixtures.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/_pytest/freeze_support.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/_pytest/helpconfig.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/pygments/lexers/_lilypond_builtins.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/pygments/lexers/_lua_builtins.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/pygments/lexers/_luau_builtins.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/_pytest/hookspec.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/pygments/lexers/_mapping.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/_pytest/junitxml.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/pygments/lexers/_mql_builtins.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/_pytest/legacypath.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/_pytest/logging.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/pygments/lexers/_mysql_builtins.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/_pytest/main.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/pygments/lexers/_openedge_builtins.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/_pytest/monkeypatch.py\n/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto/.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/pygments/lexers/_php_builtins.py\n(Results {"parentUuid":"c7e402b8-74f4-42ae-bb6f-b44d7bdd8b93","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"037faac4-a90e-48f6-9041-5732c00f999d","agentId":"a4168095d3318bdca","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01FoMK6zmBeBUBQMDqAUE7me","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# ep2-crypto: 5-Minute BTC Prediction Engine\n     2→\n     3→## Project Overview\n     4→\n     5→ep2-crypto is a multi-edge Bitcoin price prediction system targeting 5-minute directional forecasts on BTC/USDT perpetual futures. It combines order flow microstructure, cross-market lead-lag, regime-adaptive modeling, and confidence gating to achieve a tradeable edge.\n     6→\n     7→**Realistic expectations** (from 500K+ words of research):\n     8→- Directional accuracy: 52-56% at 5-min horizon\n     9→- Backtest-to-live Sharpe degradation: 50-70% (need Sharpe >2.0 in backtest to survive)\n    10→- Round-trip costs: 8-12 bps minimum\n    11→- Alpha half-life: 1-6 months for ML patterns\n    12→- Optimal feature count: 18-25 (not 200+)\n    13→\n    14→## Tech Stack\n    15→\n    16→| Component | Choice | Why |\n    17→|-----------|--------|-----|\n    18→| Language | Python 3.12+ | ML ecosystem, async support |\n    19→| Package manager | uv | Fast, deterministic (never pip/poetry) |\n    20→| Primary model | LightGBM | Outperforms XGBoost by 0.5-1.5% on 5-min crypto |\n    21→| Secondary model | CatBoost | Ordered boosting prevents leakage, adds diversity |\n    22→| Sequence model | GRU (PyTorch) | Hidden state extracted as features for LightGBM |\n    23→| Ensemble | Stacking (logistic regression meta-learner) | 2-5% over best single model |\n    24→| Regime detection | Hierarchical (HMM + BOCPD + GARCH + Efficiency Ratio) | Faster detection than HMM alone |\n    25→| Exchange data | ccxt (WebSocket + REST) | Binance WS for klines/depth/trades, Bybit for derivatives |\n    26→| Cross-market | yfinance, Twelve Data | NQ, Gold, DXY (15-min delayed, acceptable) |\n    27→| On-chain | mempool.space WS | Whale detection only (on-chain operates at 4h+, not 5-min) |\n    28→| Logging | structlog | Structured JSON logs, never print() |\n    29→| API | FastAPI + uvicorn | Prediction endpoints, health, metrics |\n    30→| Database | SQLite (dev) -> TimescaleDB (prod) | Zero setup for dev |\n    31→| Inference | ONNX Runtime | 2-5x speedup over native |\n    32→| Tuning | Optuna | MedianPruner, Sharpe objective |\n    33→| Testing | pytest + pytest-cov | Required for every feature computation |\n    34→| Linting | ruff + mypy (strict) | Type safety, code quality |\n    35→\n    36→## Key Architecture Decisions\n    37→\n    38→These decisions are the result of extensive research (49 files in `research/`). Do NOT change them without reviewing the corresponding ADR in `DECISIONS.md`.\n    39→\n    40→### Model Architecture\n    41→- **LightGBM over XGBoost** (ADR-001): Faster training, better accuracy on crypto tick data\n    42→- **Stacking ensemble over per-regime models** (ADR-006): Per-regime models fragment scarce data. Single ensemble with regime as input feature is more robust\n    43→- **Ternary target (up/flat/down) with adaptive threshold** (ADR-002): Acknowledges untradeable low-volatility periods. Threshold adapts per regime\n    44→- **Triple barrier labeling over fixed threshold** (ADR-008): Accounts for time decay and stop-loss, produces more realistic labels\n    45→\n    46→### Data & Features\n    47→- **Dual normalization pipeline** (ADR in RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md): Raw features for tree models (normalization harms trees), robust scaling + rank-to-gaussian for neural models\n    48→- **On-chain as regime context only, not primary signal** (ADR-004): On-chain signals operate at 4h-24h, not 5-min\n    49→- **Skip real-time sentiment, use funding rate** (ADR-005): NLP sentiment too slow for 5-min. Funding rate is the only useful \"sentiment\" at this timeframe\n    50→- **Feature priority**: Microstructure (OBI, OFI, microprice) captures 60-80% of achievable 5-min signal\n    51→\n    52→### Validation & Risk\n    53→- **Purged walk-forward validation**: 14-day sliding window, 18-bar purge (90 min), 12-bar embargo (60 min). Sliding, NOT expanding (crypto non-stationarity)\n    54→- **Confidence gating pipeline**: isotonic calibration -> meta-labeling -> conformal prediction -> adaptive threshold -> drawdown gate. This is the single biggest Sharpe multiplier (2-4x)\n    55→- **Quarter-Kelly position sizing**: Position size = 0.25 * Kelly fraction * confidence score\n    56→- **Annualization**: sqrt(105,120) for 24/7 crypto. 288 bars/day * 365 days = 105,120 bars/year. NEVER use sqrt(252)\n    57→\n    58→### Infrastructure\n    59→- **asyncio single-process architecture** (ADR-010): All collectors and processing in one event loop\n    60→- **Event-driven backtest engine with Numba** (ADR-009): 100x faster than pure Python, realistic fills\n    61→- **Numpy ring buffers** for data structures: 10-20x less memory than pandas DataFrames on hot path\n    62→\n    63→## Code Conventions\n    64→\n    65→### Mandatory Rules\n    66→1. **Named exports only** - never use `export default` or bare module-level assignments\n    67→2. **structlog for all logging** - never use `print()` for any output\n    68→3. **Parameterized SQL queries only** - never use f-strings or string interpolation for SQL\n    69→4. **All features must use only past data** - no look-ahead bias. Every feature computation at time t may only use data from times <= t\n    70→5. **Type hints on all functions** - mypy strict mode is enforced\n    71→6. **Tests required for every feature computation** - including golden dataset tests against hand-verified values\n    72→7. **No `any` types** - be explicit with all type annotations\n    73→8. **No TODO/FIXME/HACK without linked issue** - if you must leave one, create a GitHub issue first\n    74→9. **Secrets via environment variables** - never commit API keys, never use .env files in repo\n    75→\n    76→### Error Handling\n    77→- Always use try/catch with meaningful error messages at system boundaries\n    78→- Never swallow errors silently - log with context via structlog\n    79→- Never fire-and-forget async operations - track completion\n    80→- Health endpoints must check actual dependencies, not just return \"ok\"\n    81→\n    82→### Feature Engineering Rules\n    83→- Every feature must be tested for look-ahead bias (shuffle test + truncation test)\n    84→- Rolling calculations use only past data (no centered windows)\n    85→- NaN handling: forward-fill for price data, zero for counts, drop for model input\n    86→- All normalization fitted on training data only, per fold\n    87→\n    88→### Commit Hygiene\n    89→- Meaningful commit messages explaining WHY, not just WHAT\n    90→- Pass lint + typecheck + test before committing\n    91→- One logical change per commit, max 5 commits per feature\n    92→- Build one feature, verify, commit - never batch 5 features\n    93→\n    94→## Project Structure\n    95→\n    96→```\n    97→ep2-crypto/\n    98→├── CLAUDE.md                    # THIS FILE - project context for AI sessions\n    99→├── PLAN.md                      # Original development plan (Phase 0-11)\n   100→├── RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md        # Distilled findings from 49 research files\n   101→├── BACKTESTING_PLAN.md          # Comprehensive backtesting methodology\n   102→├── SPRINTS.md                   # Sprint planning with acceptance criteria\n   103→├── REQUIREMENTS.md              # Functional and non-functional requirements\n   104→├── DECISIONS.md                 # Architecture Decision Records (ADR-001 to ADR-010)\n   105→├── pyproject.toml               # Dependencies and tool configuration\n   106→├── uv.lock                      # Locked dependencies\n   107→├── research/                    # 49 research files (read-only reference)\n   108→│   ├── meta_labeling_deep_research.md\n   109→│   ├── microstructure_ofi_microprice.md\n   110→│   ├── monte_carlo_validation.md\n   111→│   ├── retraining_strategies.md\n   112→│   ├── statistical_validation_tests.py\n   113→│   ├── STRESS_TESTING.md\n   114→│   ├── transaction_cost_modeling.md\n   115→│   └── ...  211→\n   212→# Verify installation\n   213→uv run python -c \"import ep2_crypto\"\n   214→```\n   215→\n   216→### Tests\n   217→```bash\n   218→# Run all tests\n   219→uv run pytest\n   220→\n   221→# Run with coverage\n   222→uv run pytest --cov=ep2_crypto --cov-report=term-missing\n   223→\n   224→# Run specific test module\n   225→uv run pytest tests/test_features/\n   226→```\n   227→\n   228→### Linting and Type Checking\n   229→```bash\n   230→# Lint\n   231→uv run ruff check src/ tests/\n   232→\n   233→# Format\n   234→uv run ruff format src/ tests/\n   235→\n   236→# Type check\n   237→uv run mypy src/ep2_crypto/\n   238→```\n   239→\n   240→### Data Collection\n   241→```bash\n   242→# Backfill historical data (60 days OHLCV, OI, funding)\n   243→uv run python scripts/collect_history.py\n   244→\n   245→# Start live data collection\n   246→uv run python scripts/live.py --collect-only\n   247→```\n   248→\n   249→### Training\n   250→```bash\n   251→# Full training pipeline (walk-forward)\n   252→uv run python scripts/train.py\n   253→\n   254→# Hyperparameter tuning\n   255→uv run python scripts/train.py --tune --trials 100\n   256→```\n   257→\n python scripts/backtest.py --start 2025-01-01 --end 2025-03-01\n   265→```\n   266→\n   267→### API Server\n   268→```bash\n   269→# Start prediction API\n   270→uv run uvicorn sprints\n   280→\n   281→**Current sprint progress**: See `SPRINTS.md` for status.\n   282→\n   283→## Key Research References\n   284→\n   285→When implementing a module, consult the relevant research files in `research/`:\n   286→\n   287→| Module | Key Research Files |\n   288→|--------|-------------------|\n   289→| Microstructure features | `microstructure_ofi_microprice.md` |\n   290→| Meta-labeling | `meta_labeling_deep_research.md` |\n   291→| Monte Carlo validation | `monte_carlo_validation.md` |\n   292→| Stress testing | `STRESS_TESTING.md` |\n   293→| Transaction costs | `transaction_cost_modeling.md` |\n   294→| Model retraining | `retraining_strategies.md` |\n   295→| Statistical validation | `statistical_validation_tests.py` (executable code) |\n   296→| Full synthesis | `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md` (root) |\n   297→| Backtesting methodology | `BACKTESTING_PLAN.md` (root) |\n   298→| Architecture decisions | `DECISIONS.md` (root) |\n   299→\n   300→## Risk Parameters (Starting Configuration)\n   301→\n   302→| Parameter | Value |\n   303→|-----------|-------|\n   304→| Position size per trade | 4-5% of capital (quarter-Kelly capped) |\n   305→| Daily loss limit | 2-3% of capital |\n   306→| Weekly loss limit | 5% of capital |\n   307→| Max drawdown halt | 15% of capital |\n   308→| Catastrophic stop per trade | 3 ATR |\n   309→| Max open positions | 1 |\n   310→| Max trades per day | 30 |\n   311→| Trading hours | 08:00-21:00 UTC (Europe + US sessions) |\n   312→| Weekend position sizing | -30% reduction |\n   313→| Confidence threshold | 0.60 (starting, adaptive) |\n   314→| Min bar volatility | 15% annualized |\n   315→| Max bar volatility | 150% annualized |\n   316→\n   317→## Critical Numbers\n   318→\n   319→| Parameter | Value |\n   320→|-----------|-------|\n   321→| Annualization factor | sqrt(105,120) = 324.22 (NOT sqrt(252)) |\n   322→| Bars per year | 288/day * 365 = 105,120 |\n   323→| Training window | 14 days (4,032 bars) sliding |\n   324→| Test window | 1 day (288 bars) |\n   325→| Purge size | 18 bars (90 min) |\n   326→| Embargo size | 12 bars (60 min) |\n   327→| Target backtest Sharpe | > 2.0 (to survive 50-70% degradation) |\n   328→| Break-even cost target | Strategy must survive > 15 bps round-trip |\n   329→| Expected live Sharpe | 0.6-1.0 (after degradation) |\n   330→| Round-trip cost assumption | 8-12 bps (conservative) |\n   331→\n   332→## Anti-Patterns to Avoid\n   333→\n   334→1. Never random-split time series data\n   335→2. Never use `bidirectional=True` on GRU (uses future data)\n   336→3. Never use centered rolling windows for features (look-ahead bias)\n   337→4. Never trust >70% directional accuracy without checking for look-ahead bias\n   338→5. Never use SMOTE or other oversampling on time series\n   339→6. Never interpolate missing data (forward-fill or drop only)\n   340→7. Never use global normalization (fit on all data) - always per-fold on training data\n   341→8. Never use expanding window for training - crypto non-stationarity makes old data harmful\n   342→9. Never skip transaction costs in backtest evaluation\n   343→10. Never commit without lint + typecheck + test passing\n   344→\n   345→## Research Reference\n   346→\n   347→All research is in `research/` with `research/INDEX.md` as the master lookup.\n   348→Files follow `RR-{category}-{topic}.md` naming. Key files per area:\n   349→\n   350→| Need to implement... | Read this first |\n   351→|---------------------|-----------------|\n   352→| WebSocket data ingestion | `RR-api-ccxt-exchange-integration.md` |\n   353→| Order book features (OBI, OFI) | `RR-ofi-microprice-implementation.md` |\n   354→| Liquidation cascade detection | `RR-cascade-liquidation-detection-system.md` |\n   355→| Cross-market NQ lead-lag | `RR-crossmarket-lead-lag-correlations.md` |\n   356→| Regime detection (HMM etc) | `RR-regime-detection-methods.md` |\n   357→| LightGBM training | `RR-lightgbm-crypto-tuning.md` |\n   358→| GRU/TCN architecture | `RR-gru-tcn-training-architecture.md` |\n   359→| Meta-labeling | `RR-metalabeling-implementation-guide.md` |\n   360→| Walk-forward validation | `RR-walkforward-validation-methods.md` |\n   361→| Backtesting framework | `RR-backtest-framework-design.md` |\n   362→| Statistical validation | `RR-stats-edge-vs-luck-tests.md` |\n   363→| Transaction costs | `RR-costs-transaction-cost-modeling.md` |\n   364→| Paper trading | `RR-papertrade-system-architecture.md` |\n   365→| Alpha decay monitoring | `RR-decay-edge-disappearance-detection.md` |\n   366→\n   367→## Pre-Code Checklists\n   368→\n   369→### Before writing ANY feature computation:\n   370→- [ ] Does it use ONLY data at times <= t? (no look-ahead)\n   371→- [ ] Is it tested with a truncation test? (compute on data[:150] matches data[:200] at index 150)\n   372→- [ ] Does it have a unit test with known input/output?\n   373→- [ ] Is it added to the golden dataset for regression testing?\n   374→- [ ] Is normalization rolling (not global)?\n   375→- [ ] For tree model path: raw value (no normalization)\n   376→- [ ] For neural model path: robust scaling or rank-to-gaussian\n   377→\n   378→### Before writing ANY model training code:\n   379→- [ ] Is the train/val/test split temporal (never random)?\n   380→- [ ] Is early stopping validation carved from training set (not test set)?\n   381→- [ ] Is there a purge gap (18 bars) between train and test?\n   382→- [ ] Is there an embargo (12 bars) after test?\n   383→- [ ] Are sample weights applied (time decay + regime balance)?\n   384→- [ ] Is the target ternary with adaptive threshold?\n   385→\n   386→### Before any backtest evaluation:\n   387→- [ ] Are transaction costs included (8-12 bps round-trip)?\n   388→- [ ] Is execution at next-bar-open (never current-bar-close)?\n   389→- [ ] Is latency simulated (200ms minimum)?\n   390→- [ ] Are funding rate costs modeled for positions held across settlement?\n   391→- [ ] Does the backtest period include at least one bull AND one bear market?\n   392→\n   393→## Session Management\n   394→\n   395→**CRITICAL: Read `PROGRESS.md` at the start of EVERY session.** It has:\n   396→- Current sprint and ticket\n   397→- What was done in previous sessions\n   398→- The EXACT next step to take\n   399→- Any handoff notes from the previous session\n   400→\n   401→Full protocol is in `SESSION_PROTOCOL.md`. Key rules:\n   402→1. One ticket per session is fine — quality over speed\n   403→2. Never read research files unless actively implementing from them (they're 10-50KB)\n   404→3. Update PROGRESS.md at end of session with what was done + exact next step\n   405→4. If context is getting large, wrap up — don't push through\n   406→\n   407→### End-of-Session Handover\n   408→\n   409→At the END of every session, you MUST:\n   410→1. Update PROGRESS.md (what was done, what wasn't, exact next step)\n   411→2. Commit code if any was written\n   412→3. **Generate a handover prompt** for the user to paste in the next session:\n   413→\n   414→```\n   415→Handover prompt for next session:\n   416→---\n   417→Read PROGRESS.md and continue from ticket S{X}-T{Y}. [1-sentence description of what's next].\n   418→Run verification after each ticket. Update PROGRESS.md before ending.\n   419→---\n   420→```\n   421→\n   422→### Sprint Completion Handover\n   423→\n   424→When a sprint is FULLY complete (all tickets `[x]`, acceptance criteria pass):\n   425→1. Commit with message `\"Sprint N complete: <summary>\"`\n   426→2. Decompose the next sprint into tickets in PROGRESS.md\n   427→3. **Generate the sprint handover prompt**:\n   428→\n   429→```\n   430→Sprint N COMPLETE. Start next session with:\n   431→---\n   432→Read PROGRESS.md and start Sprint {N+1}. The tickets are decomposed and ready.\n   433→Current ticket: S{N+1}-T1. Run verification after each ticket.\n   434→Update PROGRESS.md before ending.\n   435→---\n   436→```\n   437→\n   438→## Sprint Progress Tracking\n   439→\n   440→Current sprint status tracked in `SPRINTS.md` (high-level) and `PROGRESS.md` (ticket-level).\n   441→- `[ ]` = not started, `[~]` = in progress, `[x]` = complete\n   442→- Each ticket has verification commands — run them before marking complete\n   443→\n   444→## Data Sources (Complete)\n   445→\n   446→Primary: Binance WS (klines, depth, aggTrades), Bybit (OI, funding, liquidations), ccxt (ETH)\n   447→Cross-market: yfinance (NQ, Gold, DXY), Coinbase (premium), Deribit (options IV)\n   448→Alternative: mempool.space (whales), Alternative.me (Fear&Greed), **Polymarket** (BTC prediction markets)\n   449→Context only: on-chain metrics (4h+ timeframe, NOT 5-min signal)\n   450→"}]},"uuid":"cdbce4ca-8661-46eb-96e3-afe86684b5b3","timestamp":"2026-03-23T13:29:50.300Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"c7e402b8-74f4-42ae-bb6f-b44d7bdd8b93","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

    1→# ep2-crypto: 5-Minute BTC Prediction Engine\n     2→\n     3→## Vision\n     4→A multi-edge Bitcoin price prediction system that combines on-chain signals, order flow microstructure, cross-market lead-lag, and regime-adaptive modeling — designed to be fundamentally different from the standard LSTM+RSI tutorial approach.\n     5→\n     6→---\n     7→\n     8→## Phase 0: Documentation Discovery (Completed)\n     9→\n    10→### Verified APIs & Libraries\n    11→\n    12→**Exchange Data (ccxt pro)**\n    13→- `watch_order_book(symbol, limit)` — real-time L2 order book (Binance supports limit=5,10,20,50)\n    14→- `watch_trades(symbol)` — aggTrade stream (sub-100ms latency)\n    15→- `watch_ohlcv(symbol, timeframe)` — kline streaming\n    16→- `fetch_open_interest(symbol)` / `fetch_funding_rate(symbol)` — Bybit derivatives (REST)\n    17→- Liquidations: NOT in ccxt — must use Bybit WebSocket directly (`allLiquidation.BTCUSDT`)\n    18→\n    19→**On-Chain Data (free, no auth)**\n    20→- mempool.space: REST + WebSocket (`wss://mempool.space/api/v1/ws`), `track-mempool` for streaming all new txs\n    21→- Blockchair: SQL-like filtering `?q=output_total(100000000..)` for whale detection (1,440 req/day free)\n    22→- blockchain.info: `/unconfirmed-transactions`, `/balance`, `/q/*` stats endpoints\n    23→- Alternative.me: Fear & Greed Index (`GET https://api.alternative.me/fng/`)\n    24→- Exchange inflow/outflow: NO free API exists — monitor known exchange addresses as workaround\n    25→\n    26→**Cross-Market Data**\n    27→- ETH: ccxt/Binance WebSocket (free, real-time, sub-100ms) — clear winner\n    28→- NQ/Gold/DXY historical: yfinance (`NQ=F`, `GC=F`, `DX-Y.NYB`) — 5-min bars, 15-min delayed, 60 days depth\n    29→- NQ/Gold near-real-time polling: Twelve Data (800 req/day free, `XAU/USD`)\n    30→- DXY: not available as native instrument anywhere free — must compute from forex components\n    31→\n    32→**ML Stack**\n    33→- XGBoost: `XGBClassifier`, incremental learning via `xgb_model=`, feature importance via `get_score(importance_type='gain')`\n    34→- PyTorch GRU: `nn.GRU(input_size, hidden_size, num_layers, batch_first=True)`, sequence length 12-60 steps\n    35→- HMM: `hmmlearn.GaussianHMM(n_components=3)`, no native online learning (use `init_params=\"\"` workaround)\n    36→- Optuna: `XGBoostPruningCallback` for XGB, `trial.report()`+`trial.should_prune()` for PyTorch\n    37→- Walk-forward: `sklearn.model_selection.TimeSeriesSplit(max_train_size=N)` for sliding window\n    38→- Feature engineering: `pandas-ta` (or `pandas-ta-classic` as fallback)\n    39→\n    40→### Anti-Patterns to Avoid\n    41→- Never random-split time series data\n    42→- Never use `bidirectional=True` on GRU (uses future data)\n    43→- Never run tsfresh in live prediction loop (offline feature discovery only)\n    44→- Never trust >70% directional accuracy without checking for look-ahead bias\n    45→- ccxt `binanceusdm` has intermittent WebSocket issues in v4.4.x — test your version\n    46→- Bybit order book via ccxt only supports depths [1, 50, 200, 1000] — slice from 50 for top-10\n    47→- hmmlearn is in maintenance mode — plan for potential migration\n    48→\n    49→---\n    50→\n    51→## Project Structure\n    52→\n    53→```\n    54→ep2-crypto/\n    55→├── pyproject.toml\n    56→├── PLAN.md\n    57→├── src/\n    58→│   └── ep2_crypto/\n    59→│       ├── __init__.py\n    60→│       ├── config.py                  # Settings, API keys, constants\n    61→│ ├── __init__.py\n    75→│       │   ├── base.py                # Feature pipeline interface\n    76→│       │   ├── microstructure.py      # Order book imbalance, trade flow, absorption\n    77→│       │   ├── onchain.py             # Whale flow, mempool pressure, exchange balance\n    78→│       │   ├── cross_market.py        # Lead-lag, correlation, divergence signals\n    79→│       │   ├── technical.py           # TA indicators (pandas-ta), volume features\n    80→│       │   ├── temporal.py            # Cyclical time encoding (sin/cos)\n    81→│       │   └── pipeline.py            # Combines all feature sets\n    82→│       ├── regime/\n    83→│       │   ├── __init__.py\n    84→│       │   ├── detector.py            # HMM regime classification\n    85→│       │   └── labels.py              # Regime labeling utilities\n    86→│       ├── models/\n    87→│       │   ├── __init__.py\n    88→│       │   ├── xgb_direction.py       # XGBoost direction classifier\n    89→│       │   ├── gru_magnitude.py       # GRU return magnitude predictor\n    90→│       │   ├── ensemble.py            # Regime-routed ensemble\n    91→│       │   └── tuning.py              # Optuna hyperparameter optimization\n    92→│       ├── backtest/\n    93→│       │   ├── __init__.py\n    94→│       │   ├── walk_forward.py        # Walk-forward validation engine\n    95→│       │   ├── metrics.py             # Sharpe, drawdown, profit factor, accuracy\n    96→│       │   └── simulator.py           # Execution simulator with slippage/fees\n    97→│       └── api/\n    98→│           ├── __init__.py\n    99→│           └── server.py              # FastAPI prediction endpoint\n   100→├── scripts/\n   101→│   ├── collect_history.py             # Backfill historical data\n   102→│   ├── train.py                       # Full training pipeline\n   103→│   ├── backtest.py                    # Run backtests\n   104→│   └── live.py                        # Live prediction loop\n   105→├── tests/\n   106→│   ├── test_features/\n   107→│   ├── test_models/\n   108→│   ├── test_ingest/\n   109→│   └── test_backtest/\n   110→└── docker/\n   111→    ├── Dockerfile\n   112→    └── docker-compose.yml\n   113→```\n   114→\n   115→---\n   116→\n   117→## Phase 1: Foundation — Project Setup & Data Storage\n   118→\n   119→### What to implement\n   120→1. Initialize Python project with uv, configure `pyproject.toml` with all dependencies\n   121→2. Set up SQLite database with schema for: OHLCV candles, order book snapshots, trades, on-chain events, cross-market prices, regime labels\n   122→3. Build parameterized query repository layer (no string interpolation)\n   123→4. Set up structlog logging configuration\n   124→5. Create `config.py` with environment-variable-based settings (no .env files committed)\n   125→\n   126→### Dependencies\n   127→```toml\n   128→[project]\n   129→requires-python = \">=3.12\"\n   130→dependencies = [\n   131→    \"ccxt>=4.4\",\n   132→    \"websockets>=13.0\",\n   133→    \"pandas>=2.2\",\n   134→    \"numpy>=2.0\",\n   135→    \"xgboost>=2.1\",\n   136→    \"torch>=2.5\",\n   137→    \"hmmlearn>=0.3\",\n   138→    \"optuna>=4.0\",\n   139→    \"pandas-ta>=0.3\",\n   140→    \"scikit-learn>=1.5\",\n   141→    \"fastapi>=0.115\",\n   142→    \"uvicorn>=0.32\",\n   143→    \"structlog>=24.0\",\n   144→    \"httpx>=0.27\",\n   145→    \"aiosqlite>=0.20\",\n   146→]\n   147→```\n   148→\n   149→### Verification\n   150→- [ ] `uv run python -c \"import ep2_crypto\"` works\n   151→- [ ] Database creates tables on first run\n   152→- [ ] All SQL uses parameterized queries (grep for f-strings in db/)\n   153→- [ ] structlog outputs JSON logs\n   154→\n   155→---\n   156→\n   157→## Phase 2: Data Ingestion — Exchange & Derivatives\n   158→\n   159→### What to implement\n   160→1. **Exchange collector** (`ingest/exchange.py`):\n   161→   - ccxt pro WebSocket: `watch_ohlcv('BTC/USDT:USDT', '1m')` for 1-min klines\n   162→   - ccxt pro WebSocket: `watch_order_book('BTC/USDT:USDT', limit=20)` for depth snapshots\n   163→   - ccxt pro WebSocket: `watch_trades('BTC/USDT:USDT')` for aggTrades\n   164→   - Store each to SQLite at configured intervals\n   165→\n   166→2. **Derivatives collector** (`ingest/derivatives.py`):\n   167→   - ccxt REST: `bybit.fetch_open_interest('BTC/USDT:USDT')` — poll every 5 min\n   168→   - ccxt REST: `bybit.fetch_funding_rate('BTC/USDT:USDT')` — poll every 5 min\n   169→   - Direct Bybit WebSocket: `allLiquidation.BTCUSDT` stream — real-time\n   170→   - Connection: `wss://stream.bybit.com/v5/public/linear`, subscribe `{\"op\":\"subscribe\",\"args\":[\"allLiquidation.BTCUSDT\"]}`\n   171→\n   172→3. **Orchestrator** (`ingest/orchestrator.py`):\n   173→   - Manages all collectors as async tasks\n   174→   - Handles reconnection, error logging, graceful shutdown\n   175→   - Health checks for each stream\n   176→\n   177→### Documentation references\n   178→- ccxt pro: `watch_order_book`, `watch_trades`, `watch_ohlcv` — batch_first pattern\n   179→- Bybit liquidation: `allLiquidation` topic (NOT deprecated `liquidation` topic)\n   180→- Bybit WS heartbeat: send `ping` every 20 seconds\n   181→\n   182→### Verification\n   183→- [ ] Run collectors for 10 minutes, verify data in SQLite\n   184→- [ ] Liquidation events appear when market is volatile\n   185→- [ ] OI and funding rate update every 5 minutes\n   186→- [ ] Reconnection works after simulated disconnect\n   187→- [ ] No duplicate records in database\n   188→\n   189→---\n   190→\n   191→## Phase 3: Data Ingestion — On-Chain & Cross-Market\n   192→\n   193→### What to implement\n   194→1. **On-chain collector** (`ingest/onchain.py`):\n   195→   - mempool.space WebSocket (`wss://mempool.space/api/v1/ws`):\n   196→     - Subscribe: `{\"action\":\"want\",\"data\":[\"blocks\",\"stats\"]}`\n   197→     - Subscribe: `{\"track-mempool\": true}` for all new txs\n   198→     - Client-side filter: flag transactions with output sum > 10 BTC as whale txs\n   199→   - Blockchair REST (polling every 60s):\n   200→     - `GET https://api.blockchair.com/bitcoin/mempool/transactions?q=output_total(1000000000..)&s=output_total(desc)`\n   201→     - Whale transactions > 10 BTC from mempool\n   202→   - Known exchange address monitoring:\n   203→     - Maintain a list of top 20 exchange cold/hot wallet addresses\n   204→     - Poll via mempool.space `/address/:address/txs` every 2 min\n   205→   - Alternative.me Fear & Greed: `GET https://api.alternative.me/fng/` — poll every 30 min\n   206→\n   207→2. **Cross-market collector** (`ingest/cross_market.py`):\n   208→   - ETH: ccxt pro `watch_ohlcv('ETH/USDT:USDT', '1m')` — real-time\n   209→   - NQ futures: yfinance `yf.download('NQ=F', interval='5m', period='5d')` — poll every 5 min\n   210→   - Gold: yfinance `yf.download('GC=F', interval='5m', period='5d')` — poll every 5 min\n   211→   - DXY: yfinance `yf.download('DX-Y.NYB', interval='5m', period='5d')` — poll every 5 min\n   212→   - Note: yfinance data is ~15 min delayed — acceptable for lead-lag detection (lag is minutes-to-hours)\n   213→\n   214→### Rate limit awareness\n   215→- Blockchair: max 30 req/min, 1,440/day — budget carefully\n   216→- mempool.space: no published limit, be respectful (1 WebSocket connection is fine)\n   217→- yfinance: no official limit, keep under 100 req/session\n   218→\n   219→### Verification\n   220→- [ ] Whale transactions detected and stored (check against whale-alert Twitter for validation)\n   221→- [ ] Mempool pressure metrics (size, fee rates) updating in real-time\n   222→- [ ] ETH price streaming alongside BTC\n   223→- [ ] NQ/Gold/DXY data updating every 5 min (with 15-min delay noted in metadata)\n   224→- [ ] Fear & Greed index stored with timestamps\n   225→\n   226→---\n   227→\n   228→## Phase 4: Feature Engineering — Microstructure Edge\n   229→\n   230→### What to implement\n   231→1. **Order book features** (`features/microstructure.py`):\n   232→   - Bid-ask spread: `(best_ask - best_bid) / mid_price`\n   233→   - Order book imbalance (top 5 levels): `(bid_vol - ask_vol) / (bid_vol + ask_vol)`\n   234→   - Depth imbalance: weighted by price proximity to mid\n   235→   - Book pressure: ratio of volume within 0.1% of mid on each side\n   236→   - Spread velocity: rate of change of spread over last N snapshots\n   237→\n   238→2. **Trade flow features** (`features/microstructure.py`):\n   239→   - Aggressive buy/sell ratio: classify trades by taker side from aggTrade `m` field (buyer is maker = sell aggression)\n   240→   - Trade intensity: trades per second, rolling 1-min and 5-min\n   241→   - Volume delta: cumulative (aggressive_buy_vol - aggressive_sell_vol)\n   242→   - Large trade detection: flag trades > 2 std devs above mean size\n   243→   - Trade clustering: count of trades in rapid succession (< 100ms apart)\n   244→\n   245→3. **Absorption detection** (`features/microstructure.py`):\n   246→   - Price doesn't move despite large aggressive orders hitting one side\n   247→   - Measure: large volume delta without proportional price change\n   248→   - Signal: potential hidden liquidity / institutional activity\n   249→\n   250→### Documentation references\n   251→- Binance aggTrade `m` field: `true` = buyer is market maker (i.e., trade was a sell aggression)\n   252→- Order book from `watch_order_book`: `ob['bids']` = [[price, amount], ...], `ob['asks']` = [[price, amount], ...]\n   253→\n   254→### Verification\n   255→- [ ] Order book imbalance correlates with short-term price direction (basic sanity check)\n   256→- [ ] Volume delta calculation matches manual spot-check\n   257→- [ ] Features update in real-time as new data arrives\n   258→- [ ] No look-ahead bias in feature calculations (features only use data available at calculation time)\n   259→\n   260→---\n   261→\n   262→## Phase 5: Feature Engineering — On-Chain & Cross-Market Edges\n   263→\n   264→### What to implement\n   265→1. **On-chain features** (`features/onchain.py`):\n   266→   - Whale flow score: net BTC moved to/from exchange addresses in rolling 30-min window\n   267→   - Mempool pressure: mempool size rate of change, fee spike detection\n   268→   - Large tx momentum: count and total value of >10 BTC transactions in last 15 min\n   269→   - Exchange balance delta: change in known exchange address balances (approximation)\n   270→   - Fear & Greed momentum: rate of change of index (not raw value — everyone has raw value)\n   271→\n   272→2. **Cross-market features** (`features/cross_market.py`):\n   273→   - Lead-lag correlation: rolling Pearson correlation between BTC returns and NQ/Gold/DXY returns at various lags (0, 1, 2, 5, 10 min)\n   274→   - Dynamic lead-lag detection: which asset is currently leading? Use Granger causality test on rolling window\n   275→   - Divergence signals: BTC moving opposite to its current leader = mean reversion signal\n   276→   - ETH/BTC ratio momentum: rate of change of ETH/BTC price ratio (risk appetite proxy)\n   277→   - Cross-market volatility spillover: when NQ vol spikes, does BTC vol follow? Rolling correlation of volatility\n   278→\n   279→3. **Temporal features** (`features/temporal.py`):\n   280→   - Cyclical encoding: `sin(2π × minute/60)`, `cos(2π × minute/60)` for minute-of-hour\n   281→   - Same for hour-of-day, day-of-week\n   282→   - Session indicator: Asia (00-08 UTC), Europe (08-16 UTC), US (16-00 UTC)\n   283→   - Time-to-funding: minutes until next Bybit funding rate settlement (every 8h)\n   284→\n   285→4. **Technical features** (`features/technical.py`):\n   286→   - Using pandas-ta: RSI(14), MACD(12,26,9), Bollinger(20,2), ATR(14), VWAP\n   287→   - Volume: OBV, volume-weighted momentum, volume profile\n   288→   - Returns: 1m, 5m, 15m, 30m log returns and volatility\n   289→\n   290→5. **Feature pipeline** (`features/pipeline.py`):\n   291→   - Combines all feature sets into single DataFrame\n   292→   - Handles NaN filling (forward-fill for price, zero for counts)\n   293→   - Feature normalization (rolling z-score, not global — prevents look-ahead)\n   294→   - Outputs: feature matrix aligned to 5-min prediction intervals\n   295→\n   296→### Verification\n   297→- [ ] Lead-lag correlation shows NQ leading BTC during US session (known relationship)\n   298→- [ ] Whale flow features are non-zero during known large BTC movements\n   299→- [ ] Feature pipeline produces consistent output shape\n   300→- [ ] No NaN/Inf values in output\n   301→- [ ] Rolling z-score uses only past data (no future leakage)\n   302→\n   303→---\n   304→\n   305→## Phase 6: Regime Detection\n   306→\n   307→### What to implement\n   308→1. **HMM regime detector** (`regime/detector.py`):\n   309→   - Input features: log returns, realized volatility (12-period rolling std), volume change rate\n   310→   - Fit `GaussianHMM(n_components=3, covariance_type='full', n_iter=1000)` for 3 regimes\n   311→   - Label regimes post-hoc by characteristics:\n   312→     - Trending: high absolute returns, moderate volatility\n   313→     - Mean-reverting: low returns, low volatility\n   314→     - Volatile/chaotic: high volatility, mixed returns\n   315→   - Model selection: fit n=2,3,4,5 and select by BIC\n   316→   - Pseudo-incremental update: refit every 4 hours on sliding 7-day window with `init_params=\"\"`\n   317→\n   318→2. **Regime labels** (`regime/labels.py`):\n   319→   - Map HMM state indices to semantic labels (states are arbitrary numbers)\n   320→   - Sort by volatility: lowest vol state = mean-reverting, highest = volatile\n   321→   - Provide regime probability distribution (not just hard label)\n   322→   - Regime transition probability: extract from `model.transmat_` for \"regime about to change\" signal\n   323→\n   324→### Verification\n   325→- [ ] 3 distinct regimes visible when plotted against price history\n   326→- [ ] Regime labels are stable (same market conditions → same regime across refits)\n   327→- [ ] Regime transitions align with known market events (e.g., CPI releases, ETF approvals)\n   328→- [ ] Regime probabilities sum to 1.0\n   329→\n   330→---\n   331→\n   332→## Phase 7: Models — Direction & Magnitude\n   333→\n   334→### What to implement\n   335→1. **XGBoost direction classifier** (`models/xgb_direction.py`):\n   336→   - Target: 3-class classification (up > +0.1%, down < -0.1%, flat)\n   337→   - One model per regime (3 regimes × 1 XGBoost = 3 models)\n   338→   - Features: full feature pipeline output\n   339→   - Training: sliding window walk-forward, retrain every 24h on 14-day window\n   340→   - Incremental update: `model.fit(X_new, y_new, xgb_model=model.get_booster())`\n   341→   - Feature importance tracking: log top 20 features per regime per retrain\n   342→\n   343→2. **GRU magnitude predictor** (`models/gru_magnitude.py`):\n   344→   - Target: predicted 5-min return magnitude (regression)\n   345→   - One model per regime (3 regimes × 1 GRU = 3 models)\n   346→   - Architecture: `GRU(input_size=N, hidden_size=64, num_layers=2, batch_first=True)` → `Linear(64, 1)`\n   347→   - Sequence length: 24 steps (2 hours of 5-min candles) — tune with Optuna\n   348→   - Training: sliding window, retrain every 24h, gradient clipping at 1.0\n   349→   - Never shuffle DataLoader\n   350→\n   351→3. **Regime-routed ensemble** (`models/ensemble.py`):\n   352→   - Input: current regime (from Phase 6), feature matrix\n   353→   - Route to regime-specific XGBoost + GRU pair\n   354→   - XGBoost outputs: direction (up/down/flat) + confidence (probability)\n   355→   - GRU outputs: predicted return magnitude\n   356→   - Combined signal: `direction × magnitude × confidence`\n   357→   - Confidence threshold: only emit signal when XGBoost confidence > 0.6\n   358→   - Disagreement handling: if XGBoost says up but GRU predicts negative magnitude → no signal\n   359→\n   360→### Verification\n   361→- [ ] Each regime-specific model trained on filtered data (only samples from that regime)\n   362→- [ ] Walk-forward validation shows >52% directional accuracy (above random baseline)\n   363→- [ ] Feature importance differs meaningfully across regimes\n   364→- [ ] Ensemble disagreement rate is tracked and logged\n   365→- [ ] No look-ahead bias: verify test predictions only use training data available before test timestamp\n   366→\n   367→---\n   368→\n   369→## Phase 8: Hyperparameter Tuning\n   370→\n   371→### What to implement\n   372→1. **Optuna integration** (`models/tuning.py`):\n   373→   - XGBoost search space:\n   374→     ```python\n   375→     max_depth: suggest_int(3, 12)\n   376→     learning_rate: suggest_float(0.01, 0.3, log=True)\n   377→     min_child_weight: suggest_int(1, 250)\n   378→     subsample: suggest_float(0.5, 1.0)\n   379→     colsample_bytree: suggest_float(0.5, 1.0)\n   380→     reg_lambda: suggest_float(0.001, 25.0, log=True)\n   381→     reg_alpha: suggest_float(0.001, 25.0, log=True)\n   382→     ```\n   383→   - GRU search space:\n   384→     ```python\n   385→     hidden_size: suggest_int(32, 256)\n   386→     num_layers: suggest_int(1, 3)\n   387→     lr: suggest_float(1e-5, 1e-2, log=True)\n   388→     dropout: suggest_float(0.1, 0.5)\n   389→     seq_len: suggest_int(12, 60)\n   390→     ```\n   391→   - HMM: tune `n_components` (2-5) by BIC\n   392→   - Use `MedianPruner(n_startup_trials=5, n_warmup_steps=10)` for both\n   393→   - Use `XGBoostPruningCallback` for XGBoost specifically\n   394→   - Objective: maximize walk-forward Sharpe ratio (not just accuracy)\n   395→\n   396→2. **Feature selection via tsfresh** (offline, one-time):\n   397→   - Run `extract_features` with `EfficientFCParameters` on historical data\n   398→   - Identify top statistical features (autocorrelation lags, entropy, etc.)\n   399→   - Implement top 10-15 discovered features manually in the live feature pipeline\n   400→\n   401→### Verification\n   402→- [ ] Optuna study completes 50+ trials per model\n   403→- [ ] Best hyperparameters improve Sharpe over defaults\n   404→- [ ] Pruning correctly stops poor trials early\n   405→- [ ] tsfresh features that made the cut are documented\n   406→\n   407→---\n   408→\n   409→## Phase 9: Backtesting Framework\n   410→\n   411→### What to implement\n   412→1. **Walk-forward engine** (`backtest/walk_forward.py`):\n   413→   - Custom implementation (not just sklearn TimeSeriesSplit):\n   414→     ```python\n   415→     walk_forward_validate(X, y, model, train_size=4032, test_size=288, step_size=288, gap=1)\n   416→     # 4032 = 14 days of 5-min candles, 288 = 1 day, gap=1 to prevent leakage\n   417→     ```\n   418→   - Sliding window (not expanding) — crypto regimes shift too fast\n   419→   - Re-detect regime at each step\n   420→   - Retrain regime-specific models at each step\n   421→\n   422→2. **Execution simulator** (`backtest/simulator.py`):\n   423→   - Slippage model: 0.01-0.05% per trade (configurable)\n   424→   - Transaction fees: 0.04% maker / 0.06% taker (Binance futures)\n   425→   - Latency simulation: 50-200ms delay between signal and execution\n   426→   - Position sizing: Kelly criterion or fixed fractional\n   427→   - No trading during regime transitions (confidence < threshold)\n   428→\n   429→3. **Metrics** (`backtest/metrics.py`):\n   430→   - Directional accuracy (per regime)\n   431→   - Sharpe ratio (annualized)\n   432→   - Max drawdown\n   433→   - Profit factor\n   434→   - Win rate, average win/loss ratio\n   435→   - Calmar ratio\n   436→   - Trade count per day\n   437→   - Regime accuracy (predicted vs actual)\n   438→\n   439→### Verification\n   440→- [ ] Backtest on 30+ days of historical data\n   441→- [ ] Results include transaction costs (no \"zero-cost\" delusion)\n   442→- [ ] Sharpe > 0 after costs (basic sanity)\n   443→- [ ] Compare against baselines: buy-and-hold, momentum, random\n   444→- [ ] Metrics breakdown per regime shows which regimes are profitable\n   445→\n   446→---\n   447→\n   448→## Phase 10: API & Live Prediction\n   449→\n   450→### What to implement\n   451→1. **FastAPI server** (`api/server.py`):\n   452→   - `GET /predict` — returns current prediction (direction, magnitude, confidence, regime)\n   453→   - `GET /health` — checks all data streams are alive, models are loaded, last prediction timestamp\n   454→   - `GET /metrics` — live accuracy tracking, rolling Sharpe\n   455→   - `GET /regime` — current regime + transition probabilities\n   456→   - All responses include timestamps and staleness warnings\n   457→\n   458→2. **Live prediction loop** (`scripts/live.py`):\n   459→   - Async event loop running all collectors\n   460→   - Feature pipeline triggers on each new 5-min candle close\n   461→   - Regime detection updates\n   462→   - Model inference → prediction\n   463→   - Store prediction + actual outcome for live accuracy tracking\n   464→   - Auto-retrain models every 24h on latest data\n   465→\n   466→### Verification\n   467→- [ ] API responds in < 100ms\n   468→- [ ] Health endpoint actually checks dependencies (not just returns \"ok\")\n   469→- [ ] Predictions emit within 1 second of candle close\n   470→- [ ] Live accuracy tracking matches backtest expectations (within reason)\n   471→- [ ] Graceful degradation: if one data source fails, system still produces predictions (with lower confidence)\n   472→\n   473→---\n   474→\n   475→## Phase 11: Historical Backfill & Full Validation\n   476→\n   477→### What to implement\n   478→1. **Historical data collection** (`scripts/collect_history.py`):\n   479→   - Binance REST: fetch 30-60 days of 1-min OHLCV via `exchange.fetch_ohlcv()`\n   480→   - Bybit REST: backfill OI history (`fetch_open_interest_history`) and funding rate history\n   481→   - yfinance: backfill NQ, Gold, DXY 5-min data (limited to 60 days)\n   482→   - Note: order book and trade-level data cannot be backfilled — microstructure features start from collection date\n   483→\n   484→2. **Full system validation**:\n   485→   - Run complete pipeline: ingest → features → regime → models → backtest\n   486→   - Compare regime detection against known market events\n   487→   - Validate that each edge contributes independently (ablation study):\n   488→     - Model with all features vs model without microstructure\n   489→     - Model with all features vs model without on-chain\n   490→     - Model with all features vs model without cross-market\n   491→     - Model with all features vs model without regime routing\n   492→\n   493→### Verification\n   494→- [ ] Each edge shows positive marginal contribution in ablation study\n   495→- [ ] Full system Sharpe > any single-edge system\n   496→- [ ] No edge has negative contribution (remove if so)\n   497→- [ ] System handles missing data gracefully (e.g., no on-chain data for first 30 days)\n   498→\n   499→---\n   500→\n   501→## Execution Order & Dependencies\n   502→\n   503→```\n   504→Phase 1 (Foundation)\n   505→  ↓\n   506→Phase 2 (Exchange Ingestion) ──────┐\n   507→  ↓                                 │\n   508→Phase 3 (On-Chain + Cross-Market) ─┤\n   509→  ↓                                 │\n   510→Phase 4 (Microstructure Features) ──┤── can partially parallelize\n   511→  ↓                                 │\n   512→Phase 5 (On-Chain + Cross Features)┘\n   513→  ↓\n   514→Phase 6 (Regime Detection)\n   515→  ↓\n   516→Phase 7 (Models)\n   517→  ↓\n   518→Phase 8 (Tuning)\n   519→  ↓\n   520→Phase 9 (Backtesting)\n   521→  ↓\n   522→Phase 10 (API + Live)\n   523→  ↓\n   524→Phase 11 (Validation + Ablation)\n   525→```\n   526→\n   527→Phases 2-5 can overlap: start collecting data in Phase 2-3 while building features in Phase 4-5. Models (Phase 7) need data from all feature phases.\n   528→\n   529→---\n   530→\n   531→## Key Design Decisions\n   532→\n   533→1. **Sliding window, not expanding** — crypto non-stationarity means old data hurts more than helps\n   534→2. **Per-regime models** — a trending market model is useless in a ranging market\n   535→3. **Confidence gating** — no signal is better than a low-confidence signal\n   536→4. **Magnitude + direction separation** — XGBoost excels at classification, GRU at regression\n   537→5. **15-min delay on cross-market is acceptable** — the lead-lag relationship operates on minutes-to-hours, not seconds\n   538→6. **No exchange flow data** — no free API exists; we approximate via address monitoring\n   539→7. **SQLite for dev** — zero setup, switch to TimescaleDB when moving to production\n   540→8. **Feature normalization via rolling z-score** — prevents global normalization look-ahead bias\n   541→"}]},"uuid":"b1627169-c5f3-4926-99bc-3cac7547bf6a","timestamp":"2026-03-23T13:29:50.666Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"bfeca0d5-8b91-4a8d-b384-fdac78962bc8","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

Research across multiple reports consistently showed LightGBM outperforms XGBoost on 5-min crypto prediction tasks.\n    10→\n    11→### Decision\n    12→Use LightGBM as the primary gradient boosting classifier.\n    13→\n    14→### Consequences\n    15→- **Positive**: 0.5-1.5% accuracy improvement on 5-min crypto data\n    16→- **Positive**: Faster training (leaf-wise growth vs level-wise)\n    17→- **Positive**: Native categorical feature support\n    18→- **Positive**: Lower memory footprint\n    19→- **Negative**: Slightly different API from XGBoost (minor migration effort)\n    20→- **Negative**: Can overfit more easily with small data (mitigated by `min_child_samples=50`)\n    21→\n    22→### Alternatives Considered\n    23→- **XGBoost**: Slower, slightly lower accuracy on this specific task. Well-documented but no advantage here.\n    24→- **TabNet**: Self-attention mechanism promising but inconsistent results, harder to tune, 2-3x slower inference.\n    25→- **Random Forest**: Baseline model, consistently outperformed by boosting.\n    26→\n    27→### Research Source\n    28→- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md` section \"Core Model: LightGBM + Stacking Ensemble\"\n    29→- Multiple research files confirming LightGBM > XGBoost on crypto tick data\n    30→\n    31→---\n    32→\n    33→## ADR-002: Ternary Target over Binary\n    34→\n    35→**Date**: 2026-03-23\n    36→**Status**: Accepted\n    37→\n    38→### Context\n    39→The original plan used binary classification (up/down). Research showed this forces the model to make predictions during low-volatility periods where no tradeable edge exists.\n    40→\n    41→### Decision\n    42→Use ternary classification: UP (return > +threshold), DOWN (return < -threshold), FLAT (within threshold). The threshold is adaptive per regime.\n    43→\n    44→### Consequences\n    45→- **Positive**: Acknowledges untradeable low-volatility periods\n    46→- **Positive**: Reduces false signals during quiet markets\n    47→- **Positive**: Adaptive threshold adjusts to current market conditions\n    48→- **Negative**: Three-class problem is harder than binary\n    49→- **Negative**: Class imbalance (FLAT may dominate in low-vol regimes)\n    50→- **Negative**: Threshold selection adds a hyperparameter\n    51→\n    52→### Alternatives Considered\n    53→- **Binary (up/down)**: Simpler but forces predictions during untradeable periods\n    54→- **Regression (continuous returns)**: Harder to calibrate, confidence gating less natural\n    55→- **Binary + volatility filter**: Two-step approach, less elegant than integrated ternary\n    56→\n    57→### Research Source\n    58→- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md` section \"Revised Tech Stack\" (Target row)\n    59→- Research on Lopez de Prado's triple barrier method\n    60→\n    61→---\n    62→\n    63→## ADR-003: Sliding Window over Expanding Window\n    64→\n    65→**Date**: 2026-03-23\n    66→**Status**: Accepted\n    67→\n    68→### Context\n    69→Standard walk-forward validation uses expanding windows (all historical data). Crypto markets exhibit strong non-stationarity where patterns from months ago may be counterproductive.\n    70→\n    71→### Decision\n    72→Use 14-day sliding windows for training. Old data is dropped, not accumulated.\n    73→\n    74→### Consequences\n    75→- **Positive**: Model adapts to current market regime faster\n    76→- **Positive**: Training time stays constant (not growing)\n    77→- **Positive**: Reduces impact of regime changes from distant past\n    78→- **Negative**: Less training data per fold (4,032 bars vs potentially 100K+)\n    79→- **Negative**: May miss rare but important patterns (e.g., flash crash behavior)\n    80→\n    81→### Alternatives Considered\n    82→- **Expanding window**: Standard approach, but crypto non-stationarity means old data hurts\n    83→- **Weighted expanding**: Decay weight on old samples. More complex, marginal benefit over sliding\n    84→- **21-day window**: Research showed >21 days dilutes signal in crypto\n    85→- **7-day window**: Too little data, model underfits\n    86→\n    87→### Research Source\n    88→- `BACKTESTING_PLAN.md` section \"Walk-Forward Validation Protocol\"\n    89→- Research consensus: \"Recency premium in crypto; >21 days dilutes signal\"\n    90→\n    91→---\n    92→\n    93→## ADR-004: On-Chain as Regime Context Only\n    94→\n    95→**Date**: 2026-03-23\n    96→**Status**: Accepted\n    97→\n    98→### Context\n    99→The original plan used on-chain data (whale flows, mempool, exchange balances) as primary prediction signals. Research revealed these signals operate at 4h-24h timescales, not 5-min.\n   100→\n   101→### Decision\n   102→Downgrade on-chain data to regime context only. Use mempool whale detection (>10 BTC to known exchange addresses) as a background signal, not for direct 5-min prediction.\n   103→\n   104→### Consequences\n   105→- **Positive**: Removes noise from feature set at 5-min timescale\n   106→- **Positive**: Reduces data source dependencies (fewer failure points)\n   107→- **Positive**: Simpler pipeline\n   108→- **Negative**: Loses potential long-horizon signals (acceptable for 5-min system)\n   109→- **Negative**: May miss large exchange inflow/outflow signals\n   110→\n   111→### Alternatives Considered\n   112→- **On-chain as primary signal**: Research shows these are 4h+ signals, not 5-min\n   113→- **Skip on-chain entirely**: Loses useful regime context (e.g., whale activity as volatility predictor)\n   114→- **Multi-horizon model**: Could use on-chain at 4h and microstructure at 5-min, but adds massive complexity\n   115→\n   116→### Research Source\n   117→- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md`: \"On-chain signals operate at 4h-24h, NOT 5-min\"\n   118→- Research files on whale detection and exchange flows\n   119→\n   120→---\n   121→\n   122→## ADR-005: Skip Real-Time Sentiment, Use Funding Rate\n   123→\n   124→**Date**: 2026-03-23\n   125→**Status**: Accepted\n   126→\n   127→### Context\n   128→The original plan included Twitter/social sentiment NLP analysis. Research showed that by the time sentiment signals are processed and available, the price has already moved at the 5-min timescale.\n   129→\n   130→### Decision\n   131→Skip all NLP-based sentiment analysis. Use Bybit funding rate as the only \"sentiment\" proxy, as it is quantitative, real-time, and directly actionable.\n   132→\n   133→### Consequences\n   134→- **Positive**: Eliminates slow, noisy, and expensive NLP pipeline\n   135→- **Positive**: Funding rate is free, real-time, and quantitative\n   136→- **Positive**: Reduces infrastructure complexity significantly\n   137→- **Negative**: Misses potential early signals from viral social media events\n   138→- **Negative**: Funding rate is lagging indicator of sentiment, not leading\n   139→\n   140→### Alternatives Considered\n   141→- **Twitter NLP (FinBERT/GPT)**: Too slow for 5-min (30-60s processing time)\n   142→- **Fear & Greed Index**: Daily resolution, useless for 5-min. Kept as regime context only.\n   143→- **News API sentiment**: Same latency problem as social media\n   144→- **Telegram/Discord scraping**: Legal concerns, unreliable, high noise\n   145→\n   146→### Research Source\n   147→- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md`: \"Sentiment analysis → skip for 5-min — too slow\"\n   148→- Research files on sentiment analysis latency\n   149→\n   150→---\n   151→\n   152→## ADR-006: Stacking Ensemble over Per-Regime Models\n   153→\n   154→**Date**: 2026-03-23\n   155→**Status**: Accepted\n   156→\n   157→### Context\n   158→The original plan trained separate model sets per regime (3 regimes x 2 models = 6 models). Research showed this fragments already-scarce data, leading to undertrained models.\n   159→\n   160→### Decision\n   161→Use a single stacking ensemble (LightGBM + CatBoost + GRU) with regime as an input feature, not a routing mechanism. Stacking meta-learner (logistic regression) combines base model predictions.\n   162→\n   163→### Consequences\n   164→- **Positive**: All training data available to all models (no fragmentation)\n   165→- **Positive**: Stacking is the #1 ensemble gain after feature engineering (Kaggle consensus)\n   166→- **Positive**: 2-5% improvement over best single model\n   167→- **Positive**: Models learn regime-dependent patterns via regime input features\n   168→- **Negative**: Single model set may be less specialized per regime\n   169→- **Negative**: Stacking adds complexity (OOF predictions required)\n   170→\n   171→### Alternatives Considered\n   172→- **Per-regime models**: Fragments data (e.g., volatile regime may have only 15% of samples)\n   173→- **Simple averaging**: Worse than stacking, no learned combination weights\n   174→- **Bayesian Model Averaging**: Theoretically superior but harder to implement, marginal gain\n   175→- **Mixture of Experts**: More complex, similar to per-regime but with soft routing. Future consideration.\n   176→\n   177→### Research Source\n   178→- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md`: \"Per-regime models fragment already-scarce data\"\n   179→- Kaggle consensus on stacking as top ensemble method\n   180→\n   181→---\n   182→\n   183→## ADR-007: Meta-Labeling for Confidence Gating\n   184→\n   185→**Date**: 2026-03-23\n   186→**Status**: Accepted\n   187→\n   188→### Context\n   189→A raw ML prediction with 53% accuracy is not profitable after transaction costs. We need a way to select only the highest-conviction trades. Lopez de Prado's meta-labeling technique trains a secondary model to predict whether a primary model's trade will be profitable.\n   190→\n   191→### Decision\n   192→Implement meta-labeling as a core gate in the confidence pipeline. A secondary LightGBM model takes the primary prediction + features + regime and outputs probability of profitable trade.\n   193→\n   194→### Consequences\n   195→- **Positive**: 50-100% Sharpe improvement (research consensus)\n   196→- **Positive**: Dramatically reduces trade count (fewer but better trades)\n   197→- **Positive**: Naturally adapts to changing market conditions\n   198→- **Positive**: Provides interpretable confidence score\n   199→- **Negative**: Requires careful implementation to avoid data leakage\n   200→- **Negative**: Reduces number of trades (may miss some profitable opportunities)\n   201→- **Negative**: Two-model system is harder to debug\n   202→\n   203→### Alternatives Considered\n   204→- **Fixed confidence threshold**: Simple but not adaptive\n   205→- **Ensemble agreement only**: Weaker signal than meta-labeling\n   206→- **Manual signal filters**: Not learnable, requires constant tuning\n   207→- **No gating**: 53% accuracy is unprofitable after costs\n   208→\n   209→### Research Source\n   210→- `research/meta_labeling_deep_research.md` - Full implementation guide\n   211→- Lopez de Prado, \"Advances in Financial Machine Learning\" (AFML)\n   212→\n   213→---\n   214→\n   215→## ADR-008: Triple Barrier Labeling over Fixed Threshold\n   216→\n   217→**Date**: 2026-03-23\n   218→**Status**: Accepted\n   219→\n   220→### Context\n   221→Simple fixed-threshold labeling (if return > X bps, label \"up\") ignores the path of the price. A trade that hits a stop loss before eventually being correct should not be labeled as a win.\n   222→\n   223→### Decision\n   224→Use triple barrier labeling (Lopez de Prado): vertical barrier (time limit), upper barrier (take profit), lower barrier (stop loss). The label is determined by which barrier is touched first.\n   225→\n   226→### Consequences\n   227→- **Positive**: More realistic labels that account for path dependency\n   228→- **Positive**: Naturally handles holding period (vertical barrier)\n   229→- **Positive**: Stop loss incorporated into label definition\n   230→- **Positive**: Better alignment between backtest labels and live trading outcomes\n   231→- **Negative**: More complex to implement than fixed threshold\n   232→- **Negative**: Labels depend on barrier parameters (additional hyperparameters)\n   233→- **Negative**: Computing labels is slower (must simulate forward from each point)\n   234→\n   235→### Alternatives Considered\n   236→- **Fixed threshold**: Simple but ignores path. A trade that drops 2% before recovering is labeled \"win\"\n   237→- **Forward return only**: Standard in academia but doesn't match trading reality\n   238→- **Realized P&L labeling**: Requires a trading strategy to exist before labeling, circular\n   239→\n   240→### Research Source\n   241→- Lopez de Prado, \"Advances in Financial Machine Learning\" Chapter 3\n   242→- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md` references to AFML techniques\n   243→\n   244→---\n   245→\n   246→## ADR-009: Event-Driven Backtest Engine with Numba\n   247→\n   248→**Date**: 2026-03-23\n   249→**Status**: Accepted\n   250→\n   251→### Context\n   252→Vectorized backtesting is fast but cannot model path-dependent behavior (partial fills, stop losses, latency). Pure Python event-driven backtesting is realistic but 100x too slow for large-scale walk-forward validation.\n   253→\n   254→### Decision\n   255→Build a custom event-driven backtest engine with Numba-compiled inner loop. Use vectorized backtesting for initial signal research (fast iteration), event-driven for final validation (realistic fills).\n   256→\n   257→### Consequences\n   258→- **Positive**: 100x speedup over pure Python event-driven\n   259→- **Positive**: Realistic execution modeling (slippage, partial fills, latency)\n   260→- **Positive**: Path-dependent behavior correctly modeled\n   261→- **Positive**: < 3 seconds per year of 5-min bars (fast enough for walk-forward)\n   262→- **Negative**: Numba compilation adds startup time\n   263→- **Negative**: Numba code is harder to debug (limited Python features)\n   264→- **Negative**: Requires careful data type management (Numba type restrictions)\n   265→\n   266→### Alternatives Considered\n   267→- **Pure vectorized (numpy)**: Fast (0.1s/year) but cannot model execution realistically\n   268→- **Pure Python event-driven**: Realistic but ~300s/year (too slow for walk-forward)\n   269→- **Existing frameworks (Backtrader, Zipline)**: Not designed for 5-min crypto, limited customization\n   270→- **C++ engine**: Maximum performance but high development cost, harder to iterate\n   271→\n   272→### Research Source\n   273→- `BACKTESTING_PLAN.md` section \"Engine: Custom Event-Driven + Vectorized Hybrid\"\n   274→\n   275→---\n   276→\n   277→## ADR-010: asyncio Single-Process Architecture\n   278→\n   279→**Date**: 2026-03-23\n   280→**Status**: Accepted\n   281→\n   282→### Context\n   283→The system must manage multiple WebSocket connections, REST polling, feature computation, model inference, and API serving concurrently. Options are multiprocessing, threading, or asyncio.\n   284→\n   285→### Decision\n   286→Use asyncio in a single process for all concurrent operations. Model training (CPU-intensive) is the only operation that may optionally use a separate process.\n   287→\n   288→### Consequences\n   289→- **Positive**: No inter-process communication overhead\n   290→- **Positive**: Simple shared state (no serialization needed)\n   291→- **Positive**: Lower memory footprint than multiprocessing\n   292→- **Positive**: Natural fit for I/O-bound workloads (WebSocket, REST polling)\n   293→- **Positive**: ccxt pro is natively async\n   294→- **Negative**: CPU-bound operations block the event loop (mitigated by running in executor)\n   295→- **Negative**: Single point of failure (one crash kills everything)\n   296→- **Negative**: Cannot utilize multiple CPU cores for parallel computation\n   297→\n   298→### Alternatives Considered\n   299→- **Multiprocessing**: Better CPU utilization but complex IPC, higher memory, harder to share state\n   300→- **Threading**: GIL limits CPU parallelism, harder to reason about concurrency\n   301→- **Actor model (Ray)**: Overkill for this scale, adds infrastructure dependency\n   302→- **Microservices**: Each component as separate service. Too much overhead for single-developer project\n   303→\n   304→### Research Source\n   305→- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md` section on system architecture\n   306→- Research files on production system design\n   307→"}]},"uuid":"0abef569-6afc-4bc9-9888-f7fe632454a3","timestamp":"2026-03-23T13:29:56.480Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"35930a2c-8a76-4bc3-90d7-ba2a282592ba","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

This MUST exist before backtesting so backtests reflect real trading constraints. Without this, backtest results are fantasy.\n   341→\n   342→### Why Before Backtesting\n   343→- Backtest must simulate kill switches (daily loss halt = no more trades that day)\n   344→- Backtest must simulate progressive drawdown reduction (not constant position size)\n   345→- Backtest must simulate volatility guards (no trading when vol < 15% or > 150%)\n   346→- If risk engine is bolted on 2-3% of capital\n   358→  - WeeklyLossLimit: halt when weekly loss > 5%\n   359→  - MaxDrawdownHalt: halt when peak-to-trough > 15%\n   360→  - ConsecutiveLossHalt: halt after 15 consecutive losses\n   361→  - EmergencyKillSwitch: close all positions immediately (manual trigger)\n   362→  - ALL kill switches persist to disk (survive restart)\n   363→  - ALL require manual reset (no auto-resume)\n   364→  - State exposed via health endpoint data\n   365→- [ ] `src/ep2_crypto/risk/drawdown_gate.py`:\n   366→  - Progressive position reduction:\n   367→    - 0-3% drawdown: full size (1.0x)\n   368→    - 3-5% drawdown: 0.75x\n   369→    - 5-10% drawdown: 0.50x\n   370→    - 10-15% drawdown: 0.25x\n   371→    - >15% drawdown: 0.0x (halt)\n   372→  - Graduated re-entry: restore over 5 profitable trades\n   373→  - Cooldown period after halt before re-entry allowed\n   374→- [ ] `src/ep2_crypto/risk/volatility_guard.py`:\n   375→  - Minimum volatility: 15% annualized (below = no trade, costs 35→### FR-3: Regime Detection\n    36→- **FR-3.1**: Compute Efficiency Ratio every bar (O(1) complexity)\n    37→- **FR-3.2**: Compute GJR-GARCH(1,1)-t conditional volatility every bar\n    38→- **FR-5.6**: Adaptive confidence threshold: regime-dependent, updated weekly\n    60→- **FR-5.7**: Drawdown gate: progressive position reduction at 3%, 5%, 10%, 15% drawdown\n    61→- **FR-5.8**: Position sizing: quarter-Kelly * composite confidence, capped at 5% of capital\n    62→\n    63→### FR-6: Event-Driven Modules\n    64→- **FR-6.1**: Macro module: monitor NQ at T+0 of scheduled macro events, enter BTC in NQ direction at T+2min\n    65→- **FR-6.2**: Macro module: VIX gate (skip when VIX > 35)\n    66→- **FR-6.3**: Cascade detector: multi-factor cascade score from OI, funding, liquidation rate, book depth\n    67→- **FR-6.4**: Cascade detector: Hawkes process for liquidation intensity\n    68→- **FR-6.5**: Cascade output reduces position size proportional to cascade probability\n    69→\n    70→### FR-7: Backtesting\n    71→- **FR-7.1**: Purged walk-forward validation with 14-day train, 1-day test, 18-bar purge, 12-bar embargo\n    72→- **FR-7.2**: Event-driven backtest engine with Numba-compiled inner loop\n    73→- **FR-7.3**: Next-bar-open execution (never fill at current bar close)\n    74→- **FR-7.4**: Transaction cost model: slippage, maker/taker fees, latency, partial fills\n    75→- **FR-7.5**: Compute all metrics: Sharpe, Sortino, Calmar, max drawdown, profit factor, CVaR\n    76→- **FR-7.6**: Statistical validation: PSR, DSR, permutation test, bootstrap CI\n    77→- **FR-7.7**: Benchmark comparison: buy-and-hold, momentum, random, funding carry\n    78→- **FR-7.8**: Cost sensitivity analysis at multiple cost levels (0-20 bps)\n    79→\n    80→### FR-8: API & Live System\n    81→- **FR-8.1**: `GET /predict` returns direction, magnitude, confidence, regime with timestamps\n    82→- **FR-8.2**: `GET /health` checks all data streams, model status, last prediction time\n    83→- **FR-8.3**: `GET /metrics` returns live rolling Sharpe, accuracy, trade count\n    84→- **FR-8.4**: `GET /regime` returns current regime and transition probabilities\n    85→- **FR-8.5**: Predictions emit within 1 second of 5-min candle close\n    86→- **FR-8.6**: Auto-retrain on schedule without service interruption\n    87→\n    88→### FR-9: Monitoring & Safety\n    89→- **FR-9.1**: Alpha decay detection via CUSUM, rolling Sharpe, ADWIN, SPRT\n    90→- **FR-9.2**: Feature drift detection via PSI, alert at PSI > 0.2\n    91→- **FR-9.3**: Kill switches: daily loss limit, weekly loss limit, max drawdown, consecutive losses\n    92→- **FR-9.4**: Graduated response: Warning -> Caution (reduce size) -> Stop (halt) -> Emergency (close all)\n    93→\n    94→---\n    95→\n    96→## 2.
